After completing this book for you, my sons, and finishing the last part of the science of medicine with its completion, and following its explanations and declarations, it seemed to me that I should complete it for you with this Treatise which is a part of operation, namely surgery with hand.
Because the operation with hand is lying prostrate in our region and time, and entirely private until perhaps it will perish along with its knowledge, and the track of it will be cut off: and there are left from it only small descriptions in ancient books which have been altered by hands: and errors and hesitation occur to them until their intentions are closed and the power of it is gone. It seemed to me that I should bring it back to life with the arrangement of this Treatise in accordance with the method of position, declaration, and abbreviation: and that I may come along with the forms of iron instruments Cauterii and other tools of the work: when it happens through the addition of declaration and due proportion which is necessary.
But the reason why a good craftsman of that kind is not found with his own hand in our present time is: because the art of medicine is long and requires its author to be exercised beforehand in the science of anatomy, as Galenus narrated, until he knows the benefits of members, and their forms, and their connection, and separation, and has knowledge of bones, nerves, tendons, and their number, and their exit and return, and the pulsating and quiet veins, and the exit places of those.
And on account of that, Hippocrates said that a name with a name is much, and with work it is little, and especially in the art of hands.
But we have already spoken about him at the introduction to this book.
Because whoever is not knowing what we have said about anatomy does not escape, but rather falls into error, by which people are killed: just as I have seen many of those who claim to be knowledgeable in this science, and boast about it without knowledge, and without experience.
What happened was that I saw a stupid doctor cut open a scrofulous abscess on a woman's neck and lacerate some arteries in her neck. Therefore the woman's blood flowed until she fell dead under his hands.
And I saw another doctor who presumed to remove a stone from an old man's bladder, and the stone was large. He therefore came to him and removed it with a piece of bladder. Therefore the man died on the third day.
And I myself had already been called to remove it; and I saw from the size of the stone and the condition of the patient that he would die.
And I saw another doctor who was receiving payment from a certain Duke of our land in exchange for his medicine; and it happened to the black eunuch who was with him that he broke his leg near the heel. And the doctor hastened with his ignorance, and bound the fracture over the wound with poultices, and bandages tightly tightened, and did not allow the wound to breathe.
Then he discharged him according to his own desires. After that he let him go after a few days and ordered him not to loosen the bandage; and it stood thus until his leg and foot became gangrened and he came to ruin.
I was therefore called to him; and I hastened to loosen the bandage; and as a result there was calmness, and he was delivered from his pains.
However, corruption had already set in on the member; and I could not prevent it.
So the corruption ceased to spread through the member until it died.
And I saw another doctor who pierced a cancerous abscess; and it ulcerated after some days until its evil quality was greatly magnified with his lord.
What is this? Because when the cancer is pure from melancholic humor, then it should not be approached at all with iron, unless it is in a member that can tolerate it, so that the whole of it may be cut off.
And therefore, oh sons, it is necessary for you to know that the operation is divided into two divisions with hand: namely, an operation which is accompanied by salvation, and an operation where there is danger in many dispositions.
And I have already stirred up everywhere in this book, where the operation comes, in which there is fear and trembling.
Therefore it is necessary for you to beware of this and leave it alone, lest foolish people find a way to speak and be ashamed.
Therefore take measurement with solicitude and protection, and treat your weak patients with ease and firmness, and use the better way leading to salvation and praiseworthy succession through the grace of God; and leave off dreadful griefs difficult to cure: and lift up your souls from that which makes you fear, so that hesitation may enter upon you in your faith and advantage.
For it is more remaining for your glory, and higher in this world, and finally to your possessions.
Galenus indeed said in some of his admonitions. You will not heal bad illness: lest you be called evil doctors.
However, I have now divided this Treatise into three Chapters.
First Chapter.
Concerning cauterization with fire and cauterization with sharp medicine, divided and arranged from head to feet, and the forms of instruments and tools of cauterization, and all that is necessary for the operation.
Second Chapter.
Concerning section and perforation, bleeding and ventosities, wounds: and extracting arrows and similar ones: and the whole chapter, arranged in forms of instruments.
Third Chapter.
Concerning restoration, and dislocation, and cure of twisting, and similar ones: chaptered, arranged from head to feet, and in forms of instruments.
But before that, I must first recall the nature of its usefulness and harm, and in which complexion it is exhibited.
I say therefore, that the discourse on the quality of the usefulness and harm of Cautery is a lengthy and subtle one, requiring knowledge and hidden secrets.
And many wise men have spoken on this subject and disagreed among themselves. And as for me, I am content with a little of their words, fearing prolongation.
I say therefore that Cautery agrees with all complexions, both those with matter and those without matter, except for two complexions which are hot without matter and dry without matter.
But in the complexions of heat and dryness with matter, they disagreed among themselves. For some have said that Cautery is beneficial in it. And others have said the opposite of this, namely that Cautery is not suitable in an illness which arises from heat and dryness; for since fire's nature is heat, it is incongruous to heal a hot and dry illness with heat and dryness.
And the one who said the opposite of this has said that through Cautery a benefit is achieved in every hot and dry illness which occurs in human bodies; for when you compare the body of a man and his humors to the complexion of fire, you find the body of a man to be cold.
And I myself say this through his discourse; because through experience it has revealed itself to me on several occasions.
However, it is not proper that someone should come to attend to that unless he has already been tested and trained in the last exercise of Cauterization, and has known the diversity of human temperaments, and the disposition of illnesses within themselves, and their causes, and accidents, and the time span of these.
But there is no fear for the other temperaments from you, especially in cold and moist illnesses. For now all physicians have agreed on these matters and do not disagree with cauterization in treating them.
And know, children, that from the secret of healing by means of cauterization with fire and the excellence of it combined with medicine that burns: because fire is simple, whose action does not reach except to the part that is being cauterized, and does not harm another connected member unless a small harm.
The action of the medicine that burns reaches what is distant from the member, and perhaps makes an illness of difficult healing occur in another member, and perhaps kills it.
But fire, because of its subtlety and the goodness of its substance, does not do that unless it is excessive.
And now it has become known to us through experience, because of the length of service and study with art, and standing on the truth of things: and because of that, I excuse myself from the length of discourse.
And if it were not so, because it is not allowed to this book of mine, I would reveal to you the secret hidden in fire, and the quality of its operation in expelling diseases from bodies, by which it drives out illnesses through philosophical demonstration, which would be clarified in your minds.
And know, children, that they themselves disagree on the time when it is proper to perform cauterization, and hold that a better time is that of truth.
And I say that cauterization is fitting at any time: therefore, because the harm that occurs due to time is submerged in the benefit that is attracted with cauterization. And especially if the cauterizing instrument is for pains that are necessary, strong, and stubborn, which do not tolerate delay: therefore, because one fears from them that a greater harm may occur than slight damage done during the time.
And let it not fall into your minds, my sons, that which is not esteemed by those people and foolish doctors, namely, that the illness which is cured through cauterization does not always return: and they place this consequence, and it is not as they think. Therefore, because cauterization is not, except in place of medicine, which alters the complexion and exhausts the humors that are the causes why pains occur.
However, cauterization is superfluous over medicine because of the speed and power of its own operation and the intensity of its dominion: and it is possible that illness returns after some time, according to the complexion of the infirm person, and the location of their illness, and the power of its cause: and what is prepared in their body from an accumulation of excesses within them: and what reaches them through food and similar things from their causes, unless there is a condition where cauterization is administered.
A subtle illness in a few excesses and humors of the member, such as tooth cauterization for pain, and similar ones, it is possible that the pain does not return in that one. But this happens in few cases.
But the common people's talk is again, that cauterization is the last resort of medicine, and their speech is correct: not with regard to what they intend in it; because they believe that there is no cure which compares with medicine, nor with anything else after the application of cauterization.
But the thing itself is contrary to that and their intention, because cauterization is the last resort of medicine not because when we administer modes of healing in some illness, and those medicines do not help: then we administer cauterization at the end of things, and it helps; so it becomes clear that cauterization is the last resort of medicine, not according to the understanding which the common people and many foolish doctors have.
The ancients have said that a cauterium with gold is better than one with iron: and they did not say this unless for the equality of gold and the subtlety of its substance. And they said that a cauterium does not make pus. However, this is not absolutely true: for I have already tested it and found that it does not do so in certain bodies without other things.
And the cauterium with this is good, and better than with iron, as they said. However, when you put the cauterium with gold into fire, it is not revealed to you how much heat you want, because of the redness of the gold: and when it's cooling down, and if you add more ignition on top of it, it melts in the fire and turns into plates.
Therefore, the craftsman falls into occupation with that, and because of this, we make a cauterium with iron for ourselves faster and closer to the operation, according to its straightness.
And I myself have already arranged this chapter on cauterium according to chapters: and I arranged it from head to foot, so that the one seeking may find what they want from it.
Book Two.
Here cauterization serves to counteract the dominance of moisture and coldness over the brain: which two are causes of swelling, and the abundance of fluid flux from the head to the parts of the eyes and ears, and the abundance of sleep, and toothache, and throat pain: and universally all kinds of illnesses that occur due to coldness, such as paralysis, swelling, epilepsy, apoplexy, and similar ones among those illnesses.
The method of cauterization is that you precede the patient by administering a purgative medicine to cleanse the head for three nights or four, according to how much the patient's strength requires, and their age, and their habit.
Then tell him to make his head bald with a razor. Then make him sit between your hands square, so that he has already placed his hands on his chest.
Then place the root of your palm on the root of his nose between his eyes. Wherever your middle finger reaches, mark that spot with an inkstone.
Then apply the olive cauter to fire, which has this shape.
Then place it on the marked spot with an inkstone, while you slowly withdraw your hand and turn it. Then quickly lift up your left hand and look at the place.
What if you see that a quantity of bone from the skull or a quantity of zeuberi has already been exposed, then lift up your hand. And if not, repeat with the same iron or another one that is not chilled; until you see the bones which I told you.
Then take something from salt and dissolve it in water, and pour it on the wound, and put it over the place; and leave it for three days.
Then put the soaked cotton on top of the butter, and leave it over the place until the scab is destroyed by fire. Then care for that with the ointment of tetrapharmakon, until it heals.
They have already said that the more a wound remains open, the more pus is emitted; therefore it is better and more beneficial.
And some of them said that the skin should be cauterized up to the bone, and the cautery held until something thickened like bone is burnt.
Then scrape off after what has been burned away from the bone, then treat it.
And others say that it is necessary to arrive at the end with a cautery, so that it impresses on the bone an imprint like a form of kyrate: or an instrument which women put in infusion of small letters, and they think that vapors of the head escape from this place, and that the wound remains open for a long time.
Then it will be treated until it is consolidated.
But to me these two species of cauterization seem to be entirely useless except in certain people according to the way of fear.
And it is better for him to leave with his own safety than to be treated by me.
For the head is weakened by the dissolution of its natural continuity, just as we have testified in other limbs; and especially when an invalid's head is naturally weak. And indeed, the first species of cauterization is more safe and better for me to use, and I employ it: therefore I will work with it for the sake of salvation.
Chapter 3.
When a chronic pain occurs throughout the whole head and it is prolonged in an invalid, and he uses herbs, and poultices, and purgatives, and oils, and embrocations. And especially if it has already been cauterized with one cauterization, which we have narrated, and brings him no relief from those things: then consider. For if an invalid's head is strong and natural, and not weak, and it finds a moderate coldness: then cauterize with another cauterization under that slightly. Then cauterize it over the whole horn of his own head with a cauterization, so that it does not penetrate the skin and opens up from the bone the quantity which we have narrated. And cauterize it with one cauterization at the back of his own head, in the place which is called the "vas": and this is the location where the "ventosa" is placed; and elevate your mat there, and do not open up the bone. For an invalid finds that because of this pain is very intense and different from the pains of all other cauterizations on the head.
And I will say this about the Cauterion in its place; and it is necessary that it be a cauterization by which the horns of the head are cauterized, and the back of his head is cauterized more finely with a cauterization by which the middle part of the head is cauterized.
Chapter IV.
When pain and swelling occur on the head, or when the pain extends to the eye, and the head is cleansed with purging medicines, and the rest of the treatment, which I mentioned in the divisions of afflictions, is administered, but that does not provide a complete cure: then cauterization is done in this case by two methods: either with medicine that burns sharply, or with iron.
The cauterization with sharp-burning medicine is this: you take a single tooth of garlic, and peel it, and cut off its ends from both sides. Then divide the painful area with a broad lancet at the proper time, until there is a spot beneath the skin where the tooth is captured.
Then insert it into the spot beneath the skin until it is hidden: then tie a cloth over it with a gentle constriction and let it be for fifteen hours. Then release it, extract the garlic, and let it sit for two or three days afterwards. Afterwards, place a poultice submerged in butter on top of it until the area becomes pus-filled. Then care for it with an ointment until it heals.
And if you wish to do this with some burning medicines which I wrote about in the 12th treatise, On Blistering Medicines.
The cauterization of it with iron is done according to this method. Fire Cautery, whose form is this.
And it is called Clavilis, because the form of its head is like the form of a hook, in which there is some curvature, and in the middle of it is a small prominence.
Then place it over the spot and hold your hand steady. And you should turn the iron slowly with speed, and let the part that is burned be as thick as the skin's middle portion. And lift up your hand so that the artery which is below is not burned, and a flow of blood may occur.
Then soak the cloth in salt water and place it on the spot, and leave it for three days. Then put the cloth with butter; afterwards care for it with ointment until it heals.
And if you wish, cauterize this headache with the extremity of a second-edged cauterizing knife. And beware of cutting into an artery in this headache, not properly old-fashioned.
On the manner of cauterizing in ancient headache.
When you are treating a headache, following what we said earlier in the previous treatment and in the divisions of illnesses, and the cure does not help: and you see from the illness that what we said about the first cauterization with medicine or with fire is not enough for him, then it is necessary to use the Ignias Cauterium with a knife, until it becomes white after you have marked above the place of pain with a line, whose length is half a finger or so: and put your hand on one side, and tie it tight until you cut into the artery and reach the mouth.
However, it is necessary for you to beware of the continuation of the jawbone which moves during mastication, lest it be burned or the nerve that moves it, whereby a spasms may occur.
And be on guard and take care to prevent bleeding from the severed artery. For there is fear in its severing, and especially for one who is ignorant of what he is doing, and not studious or experienced: and he abandons the operation at once.
And I come with a reminder of the regulation of bleeding from an artery according to its own manner, and in its place in this book.
If you see that from sickness a wound is not being healed by this cautery, and you see the sick person bearing with patience the cautery in the middle of their head, just as we have narrated, then treat the wound until it heals.
And if you wish, apply the cautery that we mentioned in the chapter on extracting an artery with a cautery having two knives. For this cautery is better and more effective.
On the manner of cauterizing in earache.
When pain occurs in the ear due to cold and is cured with salves and the rest of the treatment we mentioned in the division, but the pain does not depart, then apply the fire cautery: and that is what is called a Point, whose form is this.
Then make the point with it after its ignition on the entire circumference of the ear, as it revolves; or on the circumference of both, if the pain is simultaneously present in both. And stretch out with the cautery from the root of the ear for a little bit, after you have marked the places with wax: and let the length of the cautery be ten points on each ear, and so forth.
Then cure the places until they heal.
On the manner of cauterizing in torture.
Chapter 7.
The torture that is cured by cauterization is not excepting those species which occur from phlegm, according to what we mentioned in the divisions of diseases.
And having applied the cautery to the species that occurs from dryness and nervous spasm.
When you treat this species of torture with hyssop, and powdering the head, and gargling, and your treatment does not bring relief, then it is necessary to cauterize the patient three times: one at the root of the ear, and a second a little lower than that, and a third at the junction of the two lips.
And place your cauterizer on the contrary side of the weaker part. Because softening does not occur unless it happens in a part that appears healthy.
And the form of cauterization is that you cauterize it directly at the tip of the upper ear, a little below the horn of the head: and afterwards, as long as the length of the thumb. And place your hand with the cauterizer until it burns a quantity equal to the thickness of half the skin.
And this is the form of the cauterizer, and it is a kind of small knife, whose shape is as follows: although it is not much finer than what you see: and it should be so that the knife is a little above the excessive thickness.
Then take care of the place with what preceded: until it heals.
On the manner of cauterizing in Ancient Apoplexy.
When ancient apoplexy sets in and you treat it as we have said, and your treatment does not take effect, and the patient has no fever, then cauterize him with four cauterizers on top of his entire head, and one in the middle of his head, as we have said, and another at the back of his head, according to what has preceded: and the manner of cauterizing is according to what has preceded.
And also cauterize with the cauterizer above the mouth of the stomach: and this is the final one.
Then treat it as what preceded.
Chapter IX.
It is necessary that in the drink of the first patient, there should be given great hyena and purifying pills for the brain.
Then quickly dress the entire head of the patient and place on the back of his head an ointment made from vinegar, as described in the treatise on ointments: and place it several times.
This is the correct method of cauterization; and do that in the same order as I said there.
If it is then healed through this, it is good. If not: then make three cauterizations on the back of his head, which are descended from the upper part of the head to the lower part of the eye; and put between every cauterization the thickness of a finger.
Then care for the cauterization with what preceded it.
But if you wish to add more and he is weak and endures this: then make a cauterization in the middle. What if you want to add more: then cauterize it above both horns.
Then care for it until it is healed: and make the cauterization with oil according to the form that was previously mentioned.
About the way of cauterizing in Paralysis, and softening.
Head X.
You should proceed with the cleansing of the head with hyssop and with what we said.
Then shave the head of the infirm person: afterwards cauterize it with a cauterization in the middle of the head, and a cauterization above every horn of the head, and a cauterization above the back of it, and three over the vertebrae of the neck.
But if you are desirous of a remedy for the softening of the body and the infirm person endures it and the illness is strong: then cauterize him with four cauterizations above the vertebrae of the back, and the last one along with a cauterization, until most of it is burned off from the skin, and lift up your hand. Then care for him until he is healed: and thus anoint with oil.
About the way of cauterizing in Epilepsy.
An epileptic is not cauterized unless he whose epilepsy is from phlegm.
Therefore, it is necessary that you cleanse his brain first with myrrh and with the other cure which we mentioned in the division; when he is very weak or is enduring in the acceptance of medicines.
However, if it is a child who does not tolerate medicines, then a gargling substance and cleansing chewings are administered to purify the brain, many days beforehand with the improvement of food.
Then quickly shave his head, afterwards cauterize him with one cautery in the middle of the head, according to what has gone before; and another cautery on the back of his head, and above all the horn of his own head. If the patient is strong and tolerates it, then cauterize him with the cauteries which I mentioned in the case of paralysis, and softening of the body on the vertebrae of the neck and back; and let the cautery be olive oil according to the method that went before.
But if the patient is a child, then place a subtle cautery according to this method.
Of the manner of cauterizing in Melancholy.
When the causes of melancholy are corrupted humors and thick phlegm, then cauterize him with the cauteries which we mentioned in the case of paralysis.
And if the cause of melancholy is excessiveness tending towards melancholy, and the body of the patient is humid and weakened, then give him to drink what will purify his brain, according to what went before in the division: afterwards quickly shave the head of the patient, and make a bandage after that, well-made from linen, like a circle.
Then place it in the middle of the head: and the patient sitting square, be held firmly by all parts.
Then apply the liniment. And it is more worthy from old sheep's butter. And warm him over a fire with tempered heat measurement, as much as his finger can tolerate when it is inserted into him. Then remove him from the middle of his head, in a circle, and let him be until he cools down.
Make that to every infirm person once a week, with his entire regimen being good, until he is healed.
Or if you wish, cautery him by making small punctures on most of his body, except that you will hold your hand with the cautery, and so it smells.
For this kind of cautery moistens the brain with its quality.
Then place a poultice that has been soaked in butter or goose fat on top of him.
Of the manner of cauterying in descending water to the eye.
Chapter XIII.
When you are shown the principle of water in the eye by signs, as I said in division, then begin and pour the patient with what cleanses his head.
And watch over him from all moistures, and make him sit in a bath on several days of fasting.
Then command him to shave his head and cautery him in the middle of his head. Then cautery him above both temples with two cauteries, if there is an onset of water flowing down from both eyes simultaneously: or from one side only, if there is an onset of water flowing down from one eye: and cut off with the cautery all veins and arteries that are under the skin: and let the cauteries be long in breadth equal to the temples: and beware of blood flow.
And if you see anything from that, then cut him off immediately with any medicine possible: and I will come with wisdom, which is in the extraction of arteries, and their cutting off, and caution against blood flow.
And sometimes it is cauteryed on the neck, under two bones, with two final cauteries produced.
Here is the translation:
When the tears of the eyes are old and frequent: and they are above the veins and arteries which are visible on the outer surface of the head, it is verified that this is from excesses of cold and phlegmatic things. Then cauterize with the same cauterization that I described in the beginning of the flowing water, cauterizing in the middle of the head, and two cauterizations above the temples, and two cauterizations on the neck under two bones. And if there is need of addition, then cauterize it on all sides cautiously around the eye, above the outer corner of the eyebrow with a small cauter.
On the manner of cauterizing in nasal discharge.
When you are treating that with what we said in the division, and the treatment does not agree: then hasten and give three infusions of vinegar to drink for three nights. Then gently massage his head, and cauterize it with a medium cauterization, with olive oil cauterization. Then cauterize it with the cauterizer of nails, two cauterizations, above the two eyebrows under the hair a little.
And keep away from the artery, lest you cut it.
And this is the form of the nail cauterization.
On the manner of cauterizing for relaxing the eyelid.
When the eyelid of the eye is relaxed from illness or moisture: then cauterize the eyelid with one cauterization, with lunar cauterization.
And if you wish, cauterize it above the two eyebrows a little with two cauterizations on all sides: and draw back from the two temples: and let the length of the entire cauterization be according to the length of the eyebrow: and do not leave your hand with the cauterizer, but rather according to the quantity that is burned off the third eyelid.
About the manner of cauterizing the eyelid when the eyebrows are turned backwards and pierce the eye.
The cautery is in this case according to two modes: either a burning cautery with fire; or a burning cautery with medicinal combustion.
However, in the burning cautery with fire, first instruct the patient beforehand to remove their hair if they are one of those who pluck it, until it is lengthened and equalized. But if they prick him at the beginning of his growth: then bind up his eyes with a bandage, so that they may not be moved until they are developed.
When they are developed and equalized, then place the patient's head in your bosom: afterwards mark on the eyelid of his eyes with encaustic, marking it so that it is according to the shape of a myrtle leaf; and let the beginning of the mark be near the hair.
Then place the cooled cautery in white of egg or in psillium mucus on the eye.
Then set fire to the cautery, whose form is this.
Then cauterize above the figure which you marked gradually in many places, until the surface of the skin, which is like the shape of a myrtle leaf, appears properly.
And the sign of the success of your work is: that if you see the eyelid of the eye already contracted and the hairs raised at the point of the eye.
So lift up your hand then, and let him go three days.
Then place on top of it a compress with butter, until the scab is eradicated. Then care for him with ointment, until he is healed.
What if some hair returns after an hour and the eyelid becomes soft: then repeat the cauterization over that place, just as you did at first.
If however hairs are on the lower part: then cauterize it, until it is raised to its natural place: and it will be equal so that the hairs do not prick the eye.
It is necessary to make a person take out the hairs until they are lengthened and equalized. Make from cloth of linen the shape of a mulberry leaf.
Then take from known soap and from unimbibed chalk one ounce or almost that much: then mix them together with good rubbing and make it quickly, so that it does not cool down. Then spread it over the cloth which you made in the shape of a mulberry leaf, and place it on the eyelid of one eye, or two. And place it under the eye a poultice soaked in egg white: and the head of the sick person be in your bosom.
And place your index finger on top of the medicine, and press it a little bit. And you move it as often as the sick person feels the bite of the medicine, because its biting is like fire.
While therefore this biting which he finds continues, then let go of the medicine, and move it with your finger. When therefore the biting ceases, then remove the medicine, and wash the eye with water.
And then consider if you see the eyelid lifted, just as it is lifted with contraction by fire or incision, and that is good: and if not, then repeat over it with medicine on a different place where the medicine does not imprint and does not leave a mark, until your operation is equalized and the eye contracts.
Then place over it a poultice with butter, until the burned skin is eradicated. Then take care of it with diaphanic ointment or another, until it heals.
And it is necessary for you to keep watch during the operation, so that nothing from the medicine falls into the eye.
And if the eyelid becomes soft after a few days and something from the hair enters the eye, then apply medicine to that area which becomes soft because of the eyelid itself, just as you did at first. Then take care of it until it heals.
And this is the shape of a myrtle leaf.
And know that human eyes differ in size and smallness. Therefore, your consideration should be according to this: and the path of righteousness is not hidden from him who has a zeal for this art.
Of the manner of cauterizing in the tear duct.
When you cure the tear duct as we have said in the divisions of diseases, and your treatment does not bring relief: then it is necessary that you cauterize it according to this method.
Instruct the patient to put their head in your shoulder, and have a servant hold their head between your hands in such a way that it is not moved or agitated with their head.
Then place the infused caustic in the white of the eye, or on the mucus of psillium above their eye: then apply fire to the cauterization, which has this shape.
Let it be concave, like the shape of a vulture's feather cane, from one end with which the cauterization is made: and if you wish it to penetrate up to the other extremity, and if you wish it to go up in such a way, then try.
However, this concave shape is better for your work.
Then express the tear duct, if it is open, and drain the pus from it, and dry out the duct itself: and if it is not open, then open it, and drain its pus.
Then place a cauterizer on top of it which becomes very hot.
And hold your hand near the cauterizer at the eye, towards the nose, so that your hand does not stray or disturb the patient; and place the cauterizer on the fatty part of the eyelid, and destroy it.
If you then reach to the beginning of your cauterizer all the way up to the mouth, it will be well. And if not: then repeat your cauterizer once or twice, as needed; and leave it for three days.
Then place a poultice with butter, and care for it with a drying ointment, until it heals.
But if it has passed forty days and is not healed: then place a sharp corrosive medicine on top of it, until the mouth is uncovered; and scrape it according to what comes in its chapter.
And there is another method of cauterizing a fistula, which some first ones said. Approach the place of the fistula and find it; then place in that opening a fine cannula, namely, a thin tube, whose form is this. And pour into it the quantity of a drachma from molten lead; and hold your hand with good retention on the cannula, so that the patient is not moved at all, nor does he run or bring the molten lead to his eye.
And it is necessary that you place a poultice infused with egg white or water on top of the patient's eye.
For lead burns the location of the fistula and cures it with a wondrous healing.
And if the fistula is healed, as we said by cauterization and cure, that is good. And if not, then it is necessary to administer the nostril and guide the fistula back into its natural course through the nose, according to what comes in its own place.
On the manner of cauterizing lip fissures.
Many times, fissures occur on the lip which are called "Pili", and especially on the lips of boys.
When you are treating these fissures as we said in the division of diseases, and the treatment does not agree, then take a small cauterizing instrument, fashioned thus.
And let its concavity be according to the fineness of the knife.
Then place the burning instrument hastily into the very fissures until the cauter reaches to the depth of the fissures.
Then care for it with cerate, until it is healed.
On the manner of cauterizing mouth abscesses.
When an apostema occurs at the root of a tooth, or on the palate, or at the roots of the teeth: then pus forms and bursts forth: afterwards it becomes corrupted, and the pus runs and forms an abscess: then you should care for it, and the treatment does not agree in this case, then it is necessary that you take a cauterizing fire according to its size, which fits into the abscess. Then insert the burning instrument into the orifice of the abscess, and hold your hand, until the hot iron reaches to its depth and end: do that once, or twice.
Then care for it afterwards, as we said about the treatment until it is healed.
If therefore the abscess is lanced and heals, it will be good. And if not, then it is necessary to uncover the place and remove the corrupted bone according to what will come its head.
On the manner of cauterizing gums and softened teeth.
When the gum becomes softened due to humidity and the teeth are moved, and you care for it with medicines, but it does not agree: then place the head of the sick person on your shoulder.
Then apply the cauterizing tool, which will be shaped as follows, so that you place a cannula on top of the tooth: and insert into it the hot cauterized tool quickly: and hold your hand for a moment, until the patient feels the heat of the fire has already reached the root of the tooth.
And lift up your hand: then repeat the cauterizing tool several times, as you wish.
Then have the patient fill their mouth with saltwater and hold it for one hour: and spit it out.
For the tooth is strengthened by movement, and the softened gum is tightened, and the corrupted moisture is dried up.
On the manner of cauterizing teeth in pain.
When the toothache is caused by coldness, either there is coldness itself or worms, and treatment does not help with medicines: then cauterization is done in that place according to two methods: either with butter or with fire.
However, the cauterization of it with butter is, that you take goat's butter and boil it in an iron kettle or on a brazier. Then take a cloth and wrap it around the end of the finger. Then submerge the cloth in the boiled butter: and place it on the painful tooth quickly, and hold it until it cools down: then repeat it several times, until the heat of fire reaches the root of the tooth.
And if you want, immerse a wool or cloth in cold butter, and place it on the painful tooth: and place a hot iron on top of it, until the fire reaches the depth of the tooth cavity.
The cauterization with fire is, that you direct the hot cauterizing tool to a bronze or iron cannula. And let there be something thick in his body, so that the sharpness of the fire does not reach the patient's mouth.
Then take the cauterizer, which will have this form, and place it above that tooth; and hold your hand until the cauterizer becomes cool.
Do that several times, for the pain will be removed, either on that same day or another day.
And it is necessary when the cauterizer makes an impression on that tooth, for the sick person to fill their mouth with good betony and hold it there for one hour; then spit it out.
And this is the form of the cauterizer.
Cauterize with whatever extremity you have possible; and this is the form of the cannula.
Chapter on the method of cauterizing in strophules.
When the strophules are caused by phlegm and cold humidity, and they do not obey digestion through medicines, and you wish to hasten their digestion: then take a concave cauterizer with this form.
Having two open extremities, so that smoke may come out at the cauterizer from the other extreme; and place it ignited once upon the swelling, and again if you need it, until it reaches to the depth of the swelling.
If the swelling is small, then place the cauterizer according to the size of the swelling.
Then leave it for three days, and place on top of it a poultice infused in butter until what the fire burned is removed.
Then care for it with tooth ointment, until the form of the cannula heals.
Chapter on the method of cauterizing in hoarseness of voice and constriction of breathing.
When moistures overcome the canal of the lungs, and especially when this is accompanied by coldness of complexion, then it is necessary that the sick person be purged first with soluble medicines.
Then cauterize him at the back of the throat, near the root of the tongue, in a depressed place; and beware, lest with the cautery you reach the throat or skin, except for a little bit of it.
Then cauterize him with another cautery at the junction of the neck, at the very end of his spine; and let the cautery be a nail, according to the manner that preceded.
Then care for him with what came before, until he is healed.
On the manner of cauterizing in chest ailments and coughs.
When cough and chest distress are from cold moistures, and the patient does not have fever or consumption, nor is it an old affliction; then cauterize him with two cauteries above the shoulder blade in depressed, soft, empty places. And cauterize him with another one in the middle of the chest between two breasts; and let the cautery be a pipe-shaped one, according to the manner that came before.
And if you wish, make your cautery by pricking with the instrument called Punctum, whose form preceded in piercing pain of ears; and let the pricks be from thirty to almost sixty.
Then care for him with what came before, until he is healed.
And now let the cautery have three branches: according to this shape. Why should one be alleviated with him when you do with him a series of three cauteries.
Chapter 27.
When the head of the humerus is displaced due to moisture and does not return to its place within an hour from the start of displacement, until it becomes his habit of returning, then; afterwards it is displaced by a small motion which happens as we have already testified, then it is necessary to reduce the dislocation at first. Then the patient should be placed supine on his back, or on a healthy side. Then lift the scalp, which is inside the tentorium, upwards with your left hand's fingers; and if the joint dislocation occurs towards the inside.
Then take a cauterizing instrument with two handles. Whose shape is this.
Then cauterize the scalp until it penetrates to the other side and a figure of cauterization appears with four caustics.
And sometimes a cauterization is made with a cauterizing instrument having three handles, and so a figure of cauterization appears then with six caustics; and the handles are according to the subtlety of the net.
And this is the shape of the cauterizing instrument having three handles.
And sometimes one more is added to this method, and so there are eight caustics.
Then place crushed thorns with salt on top of the cauterizer. Then make sure the patient remains calm and quiet so that the limb does not move at any time until it is comforted.
And if the dislocation is above, and this rarely occurs, then cauterize it on top of the shoulder with a cauterizing instrument having a hinge, or with multiple small punctures.
For the joint is strengthened, and moisture is removed: and the patient is healed.
Of the method of cauterizing the Stomach.
When coldness and moisture occur in the Stomach, to such a degree that they extract it from its natural balance, and multiply catarrhs towards it, and constant methods of treatment do not benefit: then it is necessary for the patient to be placed supine on his back, and stretch out his legs and hands. Then cauterize with three caustics, the first being under the ear of the breast as long as the first finger, and having a hinge; and two below, on both sides of one caustic, until a triangular figure of caustics appears. And stretch between both so that they may not join together when they make pus.
And let the depth of the cautery be the quantity of three thicknesses of skin.
And let the shape of the cauteries be according to this form without addition; and if you wish, apply a great cautery in the middle of the stomach according to this form: and let the cautery which makes this cautery be one according to the shape of a circle according to this form.
And the stomach is cauterized by piercing it with one who is terrified by this cautery; and thus signs are made above the stomach at the point according to the quantity you wish with an encaustic: then cauterize it with a puncture cautery: then care for it with the cure that preceded until it is healed.
Â¶ On the manner of cauterizing the hypochondrium cold.
When it happens that in the hypochondrium there is pain from cold and moisture, or from a thick cough, until the patient's natural excretion proceeds excessively and is cured with what we said, but does not benefit him: then it is necessary for the patient to be placed on his back, and three cauteries with an encaustic are marked according to this figure, and of the same quantity above the lower hypochondrium, where a man's elbow reaches: and let there be space between each cautery equal to the thickness of a finger; and let the cautery be straight according to the length of the body; and do not press your hand much with the cautery.
And let the quantity of what is burned be the thickness of skin, the middle part of it not added; and let the patient stand over his feet.
But if he is not standing, then let him lie down, who has already stretched out his legs and lifted up his arms.
This is the form of the cautery.
And it is possible for you, that you may cauterize these wounds with a cauterizing knife, when subtlety and prudence are with you in the art.
And take care that you do not proceed too late in cauterizing, and that the thickness of the skin is thoroughly burnt, so that the body is thoroughly burnt and reaches to the intestines; for the skin there is thin, therefore know this.
On the manner of cauterizing apostumes of the Apis.
When it happens that exitura occurs, and you wish to know if the aposteme is in the flesh of the Apis, or in its tunic; then if it is in the flesh of the Apis, it invades with a pitiful pain, and gravity without sharpness: and if it is in the tunic of the Apis, there is sharp pain with vehemence: and you see now that its cure has fatigued its physicians.
Therefore the patient must lean back over his own neck. Then place the figure of the aposteme with an encaustum; then apply fire to the cauter that is likened to a ray. And this is its form. And cauterize with that cauter one, until the skin is thoroughly burned and reaches to the siphac, until all pus has gone forth; then care for it with a cure of exiturata, until it is healed.
And it is not right for this kind of cauterizing to be used, unless the study in the art of medicine is prolonged in him; and through whose hands these diseases concur with some experiment several times: then indeed he may dare to undertake this operation.
But rather to leave it, that is better with me.
On the manner of cauterizing in Pleuresis.
The ancients have said that a cauter with the roots of Aristolochia should be used for a cold Pleuresis in this manner. And it is, that you take from the dried roots of Aristolochia long ones, one root longer than those which are found from it, and let it be like the thickness of a finger. Then immerse it in oil, and burn it with fire. Then cauterize it with a cautery one on the spot where the wing of the jawbone meets the neck, and two small cauteries slightly declined under the guilezzi slightly to the side towards the part that is below the beard.
And two small cauteries also on the spot where it is between the fifth and sixth ribs slightly declined towards the back a little bit; and another cautery in the middle of the chest, and one above the stomach. And three cauteries from the back: one on the spot where it is between two spoon-shaped bones; and two small cauteries from both sides of the chest, with the lower one being in the spot between two spoon-shaped bones.
And it is not fitting for you to press your hand with the cautery, rather let it be in plain sight, smoldering on the surface of the skin.
And now some ancient people have said that there are men who use a cautery made of iron similar to a ray: and they heat it, and insert it into the spot between the ribs, until they reach with it to the abscess itself, and let the pus exit: just as we said in the case of apostema Epatis.
But in this operation with the cautery there is a risk, that either the sick person dies immediately, or an opening occurs in the place of a fistula, for which there is no cure.
Of the manner of cauterizing the Spleen Chapter 32.
When you are treating the sickness of the spleen, as we said in the division of sicknesses, and your treatment does not take effect, then there is a cautery in it according to three modes, all of which are straight.
One of which is, that you make three or four cauteries, lining them up according to the length of the spleen, following the figure of the cauteries of Epatis, whose preceding figure we have described.
And let there be among all cauterization a quantity of thickness equal to that of a finger, or somewhat more.
And let the mode of cauterization be as we said it should be for cauterizing the liver.
And do not compress your hand with the cauter, and let the patient lie weakly on his back.
And another method of cauterization is: that the cauter having two prongs, as we said in the chapter on dislocation of the shoulder, you raise the skin which is directly above the spleen, where the patient's left arm lies; and let your elevation be such as to elevate the skin according to the breadth of the body, so that the cauteries fall along the length of the body.
Then insert two fiery prongs deeply into the skin, until they penetrate to the other side; then withdraw the cauter; thus four cauteries are made.
And if you wish to cauterize with a cauter having three prongs.
Then care for the cauter after you have released it, allowing it to discharge pus over many days; for this is more beneficial than any preceding treatment in the cure.
Of the method of cauterizing in Hydrocephalus.
A cauter does not fall into Hydrocephalus unless it is properly applied.
When you are treating Hydrocephalus with the methods of treatment which we mentioned in the division, and the treatment is not effective, then it is necessary to cauterize it four times around the navel, and one cauter above the stomach, and one cauter above the liver, and two cauteris after the spine between the vertebrae, and one on the direct of the breast, and another on the direct of the stomach; and let the quantity of depth of the cauter be close to the thickness of the skin.
Then release the cauter open, so that it may discharge pus over a long period of time.
And do not remove the sick person from treatment after cauterization with him, because it is necessary that two intentions congregate to him; and healing will hasten to him with God's help.
The form of the cauterizer with which the belly is cauterized should be a key; according to its shape: and that with which the back is cauterized, should be olive-like, according to its shape.
On the method of cauterizing Feet, and Legs.
When they apostemate in hydropic and fill with citrine water: it is necessary that you cauterize above the dorsal part of the foot at night, which is between auricular and ankle; and raise your hand with the cauterizer, and do not twist him: then raise your hand: and do not repeat it entirely.
For the water citrine will drizzle, and let the cauterizer be according to this shape.
Then make two cauterizers on both legs, one on each leg, and let the cauterizer be with the edge of a knife-shaped cauterizer; and let it be according to the length of the leg, one below the knee and another above, about in the middle of the leg: and above all the hip, make two cauterizers: and leave the open cauterium without treatment for a long time, until some water drips from it: then cure it with the rest that we have said.
On the method of cauterizing in resolving the Abdomen.
Chapter 35.
When there is a resolution of the belly due to cold and humidity, until the retaining and digestive virtues, which are in the stomach and intestines, are weakened: and it is cured with methods of treatment, but does not heal; and you see the sick person tolerating the cauterizer with excessive vigor, then cauterize him with a great cauterizer above his stomach, according to what preceded in the cauterization of the stomach with a circular cauterizer, and four small cauterizers around the navel, with a small key-shaped cauterizer: and a large cauterizer or two over the alcatin above the hips.
And if you see excessive moistures and the patient tolerates them, then cauterize him with a cauter on the breastbone and with another on all his hip; and perhaps add two small cauterizers near the great one on the stomach.
For indeed the cure is advancing, whose benefit does not stray.
On the manner of cauterizing Hemorrhoids.
Chapter 36.
When there are old and many hemorrhoids in the anus, or one, which are formed from thick, cold, or corrupted humors, and they are cured as we said in the division, and not by cure: then cauterize three cauterizers on the lower back of the loin a little triangularly under the armpit, and one cauterizer under the navel almost two fingers.
And if you think that his stomach is cooled and his food is not digested, and you see his face breaking out in boils, then cauterize him on the stomach with a large cauterizer, as before; and one on his spleen, and another on his liver, with a small cauterizer: and leave the cauter open for some time: thereafter cure him until he is healed.
Chapter 37.
When you remove the altitude, then apply a cautery fire that is similar to a ray. Then insert the burning thing into the removed altitude: and your last hand, until the cautery reaches the opening of the vein from which blood flows: do this once, or twice.
If therefore there are many altitudes, then cauterize each one with a cautery as we have described. Then cure them, with that which benefits them from ointments, until they are healed.
And if you cauterize him with a great cauter on alum, it is more beneficial for his sake.
On the manner of cauterizing an anal fistula.
Chapter 38.
When an invalid does not obey the section and operation that we have described in his place, and is terrified by it, perhaps he will be healed with a cauter.
When therefore an abscess occurs to someone, and becomes old, pus flows out of it, and corrupted moisture. It is therefore more noble that what is necessary is that you probe it with a fine probe. Then know the quantity of its depth with a probe.
Then bring forth the fire-catheter, which is similar to a rod. Then insert yourself, ignited, into that abscess and note the quantity up to which you have entered.
And apply the cauter to it again and again, until all those corrupted bodies are burned away, once, twice, or thrice, according to your own necessity.
And be careful not to burn the nerve if it is there, or a great vein; or if the abscess extends to the bladder or to the intestine, then be careful about all these places.
And do not do that unless the abscess is in a fleshy place; and consider, because it is not penetrating.
Then take care of the place until it heals.
But if the place is sealed and the materials are removed from it, and remains thus for a long time: then you will know that it has already been healed entirely.
And if the materials are not removed from it, then you will know that it is penetrating, or that there is a corrupted opening deep within it, or almost one of those things, the remembrance of which will come to its place.
On the manner of cauterizing kidneys.
When it happens that there is pain in the kidneys from cold or from gross swelling, and it diminishes due to the weakness of the person, then it is necessary to cauterize the area above the membrane over the kidneys, cauterizing both kidneys with a caustic clavicle, the reminder of which precedes.
And perhaps we cauterize it again on that very membrane. Why three lines? Therefore they will be more beneficial for healing.
On the manner of cauterizing the Bladder.
When debility and softening occur in the Bladder, caused by cold and moisture, until the infirm person no longer retains urine, then cauterize it on the lower part of the abdomen above the Bladder, where the pubic hairs begin, and with a caustic from the right side of the abdomen, and another from the left side of that; and let the length of this cauterization be according to the size of the thumb's knuckle: and cauterize it with an inferior back caustic, or two caustics if needed: and let it be done as the preceding clavicle caustic.
On the manner of cauterizing the Womb.
When cold and moisture occur in the Womb, and they prevent conception through that, and the menses of hers are corrupted, and their promotion is delayed, and pain comes to her at their arrival, then it is necessary to cauterize with three caustics around the navel, as we said in the cauterization of the bladder, and with a caustic on the lower back, or two caustics: and let there be a clavicle caustic.
On the manner of cauterizing the Shoulder in dislocation.
When the mucous humidities flow to the socket of the Shoulder, and become the cause of its exit from its place: and the sign of this is that the leg extends over the other when they are brought together; and a vacant space is found at the site of dislocation.
Therefore it is necessary that you cauterize the patient over the almond-shaped anchor of his own cauterio similar circle. After you have signed with encaustro around the circumference of the almond, as it revolutes; and so that the almond itself falls in the middle of the circle.
But if this cauter is not present to you, then cauterize him with three cauterizations, using the olive-oil cauterio large; and let the depth of the cauterization be according to the thickness of the skin altogether.
Then take care of him until he is healed.
Of the manner of cauterizing in Sciatica.
When pain occurs in the almond-shaped anchor and there are causes of cold and moisture, and the patient is treated as we said earlier, and the cure does not bring relief, and it becomes old: then it is necessary that you purge the patient from gross humors with foetid pills or with artificial pills, and similar things. Then cauterize him.
And the manner of cauterization in that is according to two modes: either a cauterio with medicines that burn, or a cauterio with fire.
A cauterio with fire is according to many modes.
One of which is that you cauterize over the almond-shaped anchor of his own with three triangular cauterizations, in this shape. And make their depth good or bad. And let the space between every cauterio be the quantity of the thickness of a finger; and let the cauterio be olive-oil.
Sometimes, however, it is necessary to make a cauterio in the middle over the head of his own anchor. Wherefore there are four cauterias.
And if you wish to cauterize with a circle, whose form preceded in the cauterization of an anchor's dislocation, one by one; so that the circle contains the entire anchor.
And burn the thickness of the skin entirely.
This is the method for cauterization in sciatica, when the pain clings to the sacrum itself and does not extend as far as the buttock and thigh.
But if it extends as far as the buttock and thigh, then you should cauterize that place on the buttock with two cauteries, above where the patient complains of pain, and your own cautery on the hollow four fingers deep in the left side: and let the cautery be a knife-like one.
And the depth of the cautery should be according to the thickness of the skin.
But if the patient complains that the pain extends as far as the toes of the foot, then you should cauterize him there where he complains with a punctiform cautery, three, four, or more, as needed.
And if the patient complains of pain being below the knee on the side towards the thigh, then you should cauterize him there with a single knife-like cautery.
And beware of this in all your cauterizations, that you do not go so far as to burn a nerve or a large artery, and bring harm or constriction upon the patient through it.
And I myself have seen one or two of those who had cauterized above the hollow and gone too far in their cauterization, and as a result, the leg has become swollen until it reached the foot, and the whole limb was perforated and corrupted: then there followed dissolution of the bowels and death afterwards.
If pain is present on both sides simultaneously, cauterize both sides in this manner.
And some wise men have said that in the cauterization of the sacrum, this is the method. Make a like samai from iron, whose diameter is the middle of a palm: and let it be at its opening according to the thickness of a finger's knuckle, or somewhat less: and within that samai, put another samai.
And let there be space that is between all the bones as much as the width of a thumb's knuckle: and let the bones be open on both sides: and let their height be almost like a knot, or two knots: and make for them an armband from iron carefully fitted into the bones.
Then it should be ignited in the fire until it reddens and emits sparks: then it should be placed over a mortar anvil for an invalid or weak person to lean on, resting against a healthy side. Therefore, burn him with three round cauterizations on one side.
Then let it be released after three days. Afterwards, apply ointments with butter: and let the wound remain open for many days. Then care for it with an ointment until it heals.
Albucasis says: We have not used this type of cauterization much, because of the terror inspired by its appearance: and therefore, we have found few who dare to wait above it.
Yet it is one of the good cauterizations for him who suffers, and finds a place with it.
However, this cauterization with burning medicines is such that you make two bones having a perforated armband, into which the hinge of its gate descends from air or iron, of equal length to the wall: whose height will be two knots, or almost as big as themselves.
And let there be space that is between each one as much as the thickness of a finger, and let them be open below and above: and let them be such that they contain themselves together, according to this shape.
Then place it over a mortar anvil, for an invalid lying on their healthy side. And press your hand firmly onto the mortar anvil. Then pour between two circles of hot water, which has been heated with fire for a little while, and hold it for the duration of an hour: and let the invalid tolerate its biting and burning, for he will find the biting to be like fire, until the biting subsides.
Then raise your hand with the instrument, and wash away warm water from the beginning to the end along with sweet water: then let it be three days.
And place butter on top of it, until the blackening of burning is removed: and let it be for several days, and pus will flow from it. For it is the ultimate in healing.
Then care for it with ointments, until it heals.
But if the pain extends to the hip or leg, make a poultice for it in that which contains water, just as you did at the beginning evenly.
And this is the method of warm water: and I have already written it in the treatise on the correction of medicines. Take alkaline and unextinguished calcis, one part of each: grind them both, and put them in a new pot, whose lower part is perforated with a small hole, according to the quantity that enters into the radius; and put another glazed pot under the bottom of the first pot: and pour over the alkaline and calcis with sweet water, so that it submerges each by a finger's breadth: after which you compress them with your hand in good compression: and let the pot be, until the sharp water descends into the lower part of the glazed pot.
Then gather up all that water and pour it over the other calcis: and let it be, until it is renewed.
For it will then be very strong and sharp, which is administered in many operations of medicine, and in the cauterizing of other limbs. Because it brings about the operation of fire itself.
And from medicines are made those with which the anus is cauterized, and also like thermises, and honey of anacardium, and lime with soap, so that both are mixed together.
And Galen indeed reported, telling the cure of some ancient man, by which he was cured of the pain in the anus and sciatic vein: and magnified it to be very great. And he said that the patient does not need another treatment and that he was cured from just one remedy, until he brought it back, because perhaps himself had gone into the bath carried and had come out already healthy.
And it is to be taken from a green saffron: and if the green one is not found, let a dry one be taken, fresh: and let it be ground much with a little fat, and put it on the spot where there is pain, or knee, or in the hip: and bind it up, and leave it for a period of three hours, or for as long as the sick person feels relief from burning. Then put him into the bath.
When therefore his body becomes humid, put him on a seat. For the pain subsides and he is healed.
And know that it is not fitting for anyone to use a cautery with these medicines, unless after the evacuation of the body.
And Dioscorides who said that goat dung, when applied to a person being cauterized with it for the sciatic vein, helps him: and makes a cauterization in this way. Let wool be taken and soaked in old oil, and let it be put on the deep place which is between the thumb of the foot and the heel, and is closer to the heel.
Then take dry goat dung and burn it over the fire until it becomes charcoal.
Then put it on top of the wool and let it go until it is extinguished. Then repeat that. And do not stop doing that until the sense reaches through the application all the way to the knee, and the pain subsides.
And this method of cauterization is called Vaccinium.
Of the Cauterization of Back Pain.
Sometimes it happens that pain occurs in the back due to many causes, or by chance, or by a blow, or excessive evacuation, and similar things, through the infusion of cold and wet matter: and cauterization indeed does not fall, unless in this single species which is made from the infusion of cold matter.
It is necessary after the evacuation of the patient with pills that are fetid and similar to them, so that they be placed on the back where there is pain, three lines according to the breadth of the patient's body, after which signs are marked with encaustic in each line five cauterizations, or more according to the quantity that comes from the tolerance of the patient by his virtue: and let the cauterization be done with a cauterizing point.
And if you wish, cauterize three times or four with a cauterizing point of the middle claw, according to this form.
Â¶ On the manner of cauterizing in cases of Gibbous Inflammation.
This illness often happens to small children.
And the sign of its inception is that it happens to boys as a constriction in breathing at elevation and motion; and you will find it in the last vertebrae of the back and knots of theirs, which has already begun to protrude above the other vertebrae.
When therefore you see this and wish to do it, then cauterize him with a cauterizing point that is a circle according to this form.
And take the cauterizing point over all parts of the vertebra equally: and if you wish, cauterize around the vertebra with a puncturing point two or three lines: and let them be close to each other.
Then take care of the place until it heals with what we have said.
And beware, lest you apply a cauterizing point to the gibbosity which occurs in a spasm of the nerve.
Â¶ On the manner of cauterizing in Gout and pains of joints.
When the pains of joints are from cold humidities that flow to any part of the body, and when they occur in the feet, according to the custom of physicians it is proper to call that Gout.
When therefore podagra is cured due to cold causes with modes of cure, and pains are not removed, then a cauterization removes them.
And it is, that he cauterizes him after purging around the joint of the feet with many cauteries; and let the cauter be Olive.
And if you wish to prick on the surface of the foot, then do so with a cauter. But if the pains ascend to the knees or other joints, and often that happens, then cauterize him over all the knee with three cauteries, or four from every part, with the same cauter of Clavus.
But if you need more of this cauter, then cauterize him. And do not immerse your hand with the cauter, rather it should be about as thick as the thickness of skin.
But if the pains ascend to the knees and back: then apply what we said earlier from the cauter, in its own chapter.
What if the pains are only in the hands: then prick around the wrists, as two lines turn back.
But if there remains from the pains in the fingers: then prick them, over every joint pricking and on the palm of the hand.
But if the pains ascend after days to the hips or shoulders: then cauterize both from every part.
And do not purge the patient with a good regimen, nor by taking medicine. For if a good regimen is done, and phlegm is purged, he will be healed with the help of God with this cauter.
Â¶ Of the manner of cauterizing in Ruptures.
When a rupture occurs in the groin and the intestine or bladder descends to the testicle, and it is that which begins to be near: then it is necessary for you to advise the patient to stop eating on his day. And it uses something gentle, whereby dung will descend from its stomach.
Then sit him between your hands on his back: and bid him to hold his breath until he goes out, or appears to be passing stool, or intestine.
Then lead him with your fingers, and mark with an encaustum beneath the rupture above the pubic bone, with a sign whose extremity is similar to the middle of a circle above the body.
Then use an iron cautery, which has this shape, until it comes white and sheds sparks. Then lead the intestine or intestine back to its natural curve. Then let the attendant place his hand on the spot to prevent the intestine from coming out: and you have already opened up between the patient's legs, and placed a poultice underneath him, and another servant above his legs, and another above his chest who is holding hands.
Then place the cautery on top of it with your hand steady upright alongside. And hold him until you reach the mouth with him: or go around him again in a different way if you are not able to reach the mouth with him at first.
And carefully observe the exit of the intestine during your cautery hour, lest you burn him and cause harm to come upon the patient or even death.
And know that when you do not reach the mouth with the cautery, your operation does not matter.
And it is necessary for the cautery of infants to be subtle, according to their measure.
Then take care with the remaining ointments until he heals.
And let the patient lie on his back for forty days until the wound is sealed.
And it is necessary that you place his food in proportion to the length of time required for his cure, so that it soothes his stomach: lest he excrete intestine during eating and evacuation.
Then when he wants to operate after forty days, then administer a well-made ligament and hold it for forty other days.
And let him be freed from labor, and from taking food and drink, and from loud voices.
For when he uses this regimen, thus he is healed by a complete cure.
And I will say the treatment of ruptures with an incision in his chapter.
But when ruptures occur in the remaining part of the belly, and are just beginning, and it is desired that they not increase, then cauterize the rupture with a rounded caustic according to its size: and let what is burned be as its third from that time. Then care for it according to what we have said, and it will not increase.
And now some of the first ones have said that the rupture should be cauterized with a triangular caustic, according to this shape.
After it is marked with encaustum, and a line is placed that is across the width on the upper side of the rupture, and another line below. And place your hand in the middle with a caustic awl.
But first, the caustic is easier and better.
On the method of cauterizing in cases of pain due to a fall or blow.
Chapter 48.
When it happens in some members due to a fall or blow, and pain persists for a long time, and treatment with medicines does not bring relief: then it is necessary that it be cauterized with the point caustic.
And let the caustic be for every part according to its size, and its softness, and weakness, and strength, and the location of the torsion, and the pain from it.
If then he is healed by the first caustic, it is well. If not, then iterate over this cautery.
Since it is customary for these pains to shift from one member to another that approaches it. Therefore you should follow them with the cautery until the sick person is healed.
About the manner of cauterizing in Leprosy.
But lepers are sometimes relieved by cauterization to the greatest extent. And especially the type of leprosy that occurs due to the putrefaction of phlegmatic and melancholic humors: when therefore you wish to cauterize it, consider it.
So if the leprosy is not responding and you have treated it as we said in the division, and it does not subside or stand still: and you fear for the patient, because corruption may spread to his entire complexion: then cauterize him on the head with five cauterizations: one in the middle of the head, marked; and a second one lower down towards the forehead at the end of the hair, and two on both horns, and one behind on the nape of the neck.
And with the last of your fingers and the cautery, press slightly until it makes a small impression on his mouth, and the bark breaks out: so that the exhalation of gross vapors from him may be alleviated, and cauterize also over his spleen, according to what has preceded.
But if the leprosy has already spread over the patient and is manifestly apparent: then it is necessary to cauterize with those cauterizations which we said in the chapter, and also cauterize on the tip of the nose, and two on each cheekbone, and two on the vertebrae of the neck, and six on the vertebrae of the back, and one large on the hips at the end of the spine and one above it, in the middle of the nape: and two on the armpits: that is to say, one on each armpit, and two on each knee, and two on each shoulder, and two on each elbow, and two on the soft parts of his chest: and cauterize him over every joint, from the joints of his fingers, hands, and feet: and cauterize also over every heel of his feet, and toe of his hands.
And beware of the nerves that are above the heel bone, lest you burn them.
And sometimes it is cauterized with a cautery over the hipbone, and another time over the ribcage, and again over the liver.
And know that the more you add to the cautery, the greater is its benefit and effectiveness.
And know that the weak one does not find pain in a cautery, as the healthy ones do; therefore, because his body is already numb.
And it should be that the cauteries are of great size and smallness according to members and joints: according to what preceded from the types of instruments.
Then care for the cautery with flour from a plant mixed with honey, and the rest of the treatment, until it heals.
Â¶ On the manner of cauterizing in numbness.
When some member is numb and is treated with medicines, oils, and poultices, but does not heal, then cauterize the numb member with cauteries, according to the magnitude of the member or its smallness.
And make your cautery penetrate into the thickness of the skin a little bit. Then care for it with an ointment, until it heals.
And sometimes it is cauterized for some numbness that occurs in the hand and foot at the spine of the back where the nerves that move that member are located; and the numbness is removed.
But do not presume over this unless one is wise in the anatomy of members and the exit of nerves that move the body.
Chapter 51.
When a blister becomes old and does not yield to anything from the arts of medicine: then cauterize over it with a deep cautery for a little bit, according to the thickness of the skin, until the whitishness is removed and its color is changed.
Then care for it with the flour of a herb, and lentils with rose oil, and leaves of arnoglossa, and dove's blood, and heron's blood: each one be part of one: let these all be mixed together, and be spread over a cloth, and stick to the place, until it is healed.
On the manner of cauterizing in Cancer.
When Cancer is beginning to form and you wish to stop it: then cauterize it with a circular cautery around its circle, as if it were revolving.
But wise men have said that the cancer should be cauterized with the last cautery in the middle.
But it doesn't seem right to me, because I fear that it will ulcers; and I have already seen this happen on a few occasions.
And it is better to cauterize around its circumference with a circle, as we said, or with many cauteries.
On the manner of cauterizing in Adubenatae.
When someone has an Adubenata and it is delayed in maturing, either because of superfluity causing it or because of the weakness of age, when there is a deficiency of blood, or because of time, and you wish to hasten its maturation; then cauterize around its circumference with small cauteries, making many punctures. Then leave it alone. For it will hasten with maturation.
If however you wish to pierce it with a cautery, then ignite the cautery, which has this shape.
And place it in the middle of the Adubenata, until it penetrates the skin; and let the cautery be from that which follows, so that the flow of pus may be eased.
Then care for it until it is healed.
On the manner of cauterizing in a corrupting evil.
Here is the translation:
Corrosion is not anything other than corruption in a walking member, and it corrupts it; just as fire consumes dry wood.
So if you see a corroding wound in a place that can tolerate cauterization with fire, then many small and great cauteries will be applied to it, according to the nature of the place where the corrosion is.
Then cauterize it from all parts until you eradicate the entire corruption, and not a single thing remains of it completely.
Then let it be for three days, and place over the cauterized areas sulfur that has been ground with oil, until all scabs are eradicated and all corruption.
Then care for it with ointments producing flesh.
So if you see that after three days, healthy flesh is born, without corruption, it is good.
And if not, then reapply the cautery over what remains of the corrupted areas.
And corrosion is healed sometimes with acute medicine. Itself rises in the place of the cautery.
However, the cautery with fire is more expeditious for relief; and I have already said its division with acute medicine: therefore, take it there when you need it.
Of the manner of cauterizing in Claws and Warts.
Chapter 55.
This illness often occurs in the lower parts of the feet: and it is a thick, filtered substance that injures the foot.
And there is indeed a cautery for them in two ways: one with fire and the other with hot water.
